1935.10.23

Italo-Ethiopian Peace Talks: French Cabinet Satisfied with Progress; British and Italian Continued Negotiations in Rome; Italian Side States Only Explanation Provided, No Concrete Suggestions Made 1

(Paris) The cabinet held a meeting this morning at 9:30 AM, which adjourned at 12:10 PM. A public announcement stated that Premier Laval had reported on the negotiations between Britain, France, and Italy regarding a solution to the Italo-Ethiopian dispute. The cabinet unanimously expressed its support and satisfaction with the improved situation in the Italo-Ethiopian dispute. (Havas, 22nd)

(Paris) Premier Laval is now facing a crucial moment to test his ability to mediate international affairs. He plans to make efforts to reconcile the East African conflict before the League of Nations' Committee of Fifty-Two reconvenes in Geneva on October 31st. However, the full authority granted to Laval by the Chamber of Deputies upon his assumption of the premiership will also expire on October 31st, compounding his domestic difficulties at a time of international crisis. (Guomin News Agency, 21st)

(Rome) A political spokesperson told a Reuters reporter that the ongoing diplomatic talks are of a general nature. Their purpose is merely to explain everything, and there is no question of proposing concrete suggestions for resolving the Italo-Ethiopian dispute. (Reuters, 22nd)

(Rome) Deputy Foreign Minister Suvich met with British Ambassador Sir Eric Drummond yesterday afternoon. According to official sources, the purpose of the meeting was to exchange views on major issues, and no new suggestions were made. (Havas, 22nd)

(London) It is generally believed here today that the easing of Anglo-Italian relations may lead to Italo-Ethiopian peace. Observers believe that the atmosphere in Europe has changed. The League of Nations' Committee of Fifty-Two will suspend its meeting until October 31st to allow diplomats to conduct peace talks before a date is set for a complete embargo on war materials. (Guomin News Agency, 21st)

(Rome) According to reliable sources here today, Prime Minister Mussolini is prepared to begin negotiations on a "fundamental solution" to the Italo-Ethiopian dispute. However, Mussolini will not agree to discuss until Britain reduces its Mediterranean fleet and ceases its hostile attitude in Geneva. Another reliable source said today that Mussolini needs the following three points to be addressed before negotiations can proceed: (1) the British fleet withdraws from the Mediterranean; (2) the League of Nations suspends economic sanctions; and (3) Italy is allowed to "consolidate" the land it has already occupied in Ethiopia. It is understood that the meaning of the third item is that Italy hopes to have occupied all of Ethiopia's low-lying areas by the time negotiations begin. (Guomin News Agency, 21st)

(London) Political figures believe that negotiations on the Abyssinian question are currently underway, but this issue is extremely complex and may be difficult to resolve in the shortest amount of time. It is reported that the minimum conditions for resolving the Italo-Ethiopian dispute proposed by the Italian government have been deemed unsatisfactory by Britain and France and have been rejected. However, semi-official sources believe that Italian Prime Minister Mussolini is now considering the objections of Britain and France and may soon make new suggestions. Semi-official sources also hope that negotiations can continue, but they believe that a solution may not be possible within the year, as any solution must be approved by the Ethiopian Emperor and deemed satisfactory by the League of Nations. Britain's role is merely to convey information. The power of final decision still rests with the League of Nations' Council. However, given the current situation, the gradual implementation of sanctions by the League of Nations may force Italy to gradually reduce its demands. As for the League of Nations, it will certainly be happy to accept any plan agreed upon by Britain, France, and Ethiopia. Rumors of secret negotiations between the Italian and Ethiopian governments suggest that Mussolini has not forgotten the Ethiopian Emperor. (Havas, 21st)

First Step in League of Nations Sanctions: 23 Nations Have Implemented, Notifying the US, Japan, Germany, etc. to Comply 2

(Geneva) The Secretariat of the League of Nations today sent letters to eleven non-member countries, including the United States, Germany, Japan, and Brazil, informing them of the resolution to implement financial and economic sanctions against Italy and asking them to participate in unison. The Secretariat also received notifications today from Belgium, Bulgaria, Estonia, Norway, and Turkey that they have imposed an arms embargo on Italy. In total, 23 countries have now taken this action. Belgium also stated that financial sanctions have been implemented. (Guomin News Agency, 22nd)

Ethiopian Imperial Guard Mobilizes: Three Routes to the Front, Over Ten Thousand Strong, Emperor Personally Embarks on Expedition 3

Addis Ababa: At dawn today, an advance force of 1,500 members of the Imperial Guard departed from here, traveling 150 miles to Taixi. The send-off was a grand occasion. They will be divided into small teams, advancing on three routes to reach their destination. The soldiers of the Imperial Guard are all physically robust and dressed like British soldiers, but all are barefoot, as wearing shoes would reduce their speed. The entire army consists of 12,000 men, including 3,000 cavalry. At midday, they all gathered on the mountain peaks overlooking Addis Ababa, then divided into two columns. One marched toward Taixi, which will be the main base of the northern Ethiopian army, and the other headed to Gogam, directly north of Addis Ababa. Their wives and lovers accompanied them up the mountain peaks, waving their handkerchiefs until the troops were out of sight. Supplies needed by the army, such as mules, machine guns, anti-aircraft guns, medicines, emergency rations, and mobile battlefield wireless equipment, were transported in batches. Italian planes have now flown within 80 miles of Addis Ababa, so the departure of troops and supplies is divided into small batches to prevent enemy aircraft from hindering them. The departure of the Imperial Guard from Addis Ababa is widely seen as a precursor to the Emperor's imminent departure for the front lines. The Emperor will depart by car or truck, accompanied by a large entourage. (Reuters, 22nd)

Addis Ababa: All evidence suggests that Ethiopia is preparing a general offensive. Thousands of elite infantry, including the guards, left for the front lines today. This indicates that a major battle in the north is imminent. The Emperor's pardon of former Minister of Land Yirbiru, who embezzled public funds, proves that the Ethiopian government is now striving to eliminate internal strife and unite all factions to resist the Italian invasion. General Seyoum, commander of the Northern Army and governor of Tigray Province, which is resisting the Italian Eritrean enemy forces, reported his military plans to the Emperor by telephone today. It is said that Seyoum advocates testing the military strength in the northeast. The rumor that the Ethiopian government is borrowing a huge sum of 2 million pounds from Britain is still very strong today. Well-informed observers believe that efforts are now being made to secure the supply of arms to Ethiopian troops in the war zone. A large amount of arms is stored in the Dara Sarah area south of the capital, indicating that the Ethiopian army is preparing to attack the Italian army from the west of the Shibeli River. Tribal infighting is making things difficult for the Emperor. (Guomin News Agency, 21st)

Ethiopia: National Unity Against Foreign Invasion, Former Minister of Land Pardoned 4

Addis Ababa: According to a telegram from our correspondent O'Chaina, former Minister of Land Yirbiru (cousin of former Emperor Menelik), who was condemned two years ago for disobeying the Emperor's orders, has been pardoned. Since leaving office, Yirbiru has been living in seclusion on his farm in the city of Adusa. Although the Emperor recently summoned him to the capital, he was unable to make the trip due to illness. Now, with the foreign invasion imminent, the whole country is united to resist the powerful enemy. All subjects are supporting the Emperor, and even criminals have been pardoned by the Emperor to strengthen national defense. Yirbiru is one of them. He led his family and servants to the palace yesterday, prostrated himself, and, according to traditional custom, murmured "Abyabyabi" (meaning "forgive me"). After entering the palace, he crawled forward on his knees. Only after the Emperor issued an edict of pardon did he stand up. The Emperor immediately ordered him to rejoin the army and serve the country. (Havas, 22nd)

Under Cover of Aircraft and Artillery: Italian Army Occupies Dagneri, Ethiopian Army Fights Bravely, Heavy Losses 5

(London) Yesterday's Italian announcement that the Italian non-regular army had occupied the town of Dagneri on the Ogaden front has partially dispelled the doubts surrounding the southern Ethiopian campaign led by General Graziani, Governor of Italian Somaliland. According to this news, the southern Italian front is not as close to Harar as initially expected. The front line stretches from Domo on the border of British Somaliland, through the famous watering hole Gerlogubi, to Dolo on the border of British Kenya. Dagneri is an important high point located on a 600-foot mountain. Ethiopian forces had heavily fortified it and stored a large amount of ammunition there. At dawn on October 18, the Italian army began its attack, first with ten aircraft bombing the area, followed by machine guns strafing Ethiopian positions. Five aircraft were hit by Ethiopian soldiers, but all returned safely. The infantry attack was carried out by Somali and Asgari troops, surging forward like an angry tide, aided by members of the Kelaldingis tribe, who had recently surrendered to the Italian army. On the same day, the Italian army bombed Burdoli, 50 miles northwest of Mustahil, setting it on fire and occupying Soillave, which is especially important because it is a fertile pastureland in a semi-desert environment. (Reuters, 21st)

Southern Italian Front: Indigenous troops from the Italian territories under the command of General Graziani advanced today in the Ogaden province after the most intense fighting since the start of the conflict. All reports indicate victory. Italian troops suffered fewer casualties, while Ethiopian troops suffered heavy losses. The battle was quite spectacular, but perhaps not too bloody, as the Italian side relied entirely on the power of aircraft and artillery. An Associated Press reporter witnessed the entire battle. It began at dawn last Wednesday, when Italian Dubat troops suddenly attacked the heavily guarded Douboli Fortress. A second force set out from Mustahil and crossed the Shibeli River on Friday morning, advancing in the face of Ethiopian gunfire and spears. Dagneri is a mountain peak overlooking the Shibeli River and is also heavily guarded. The Italian army began bombing it at 2 PM on Saturday. On Monday, Dubat troops began climbing the hillside, led by aircraft that strafed Ethiopian trenches with machine guns. The two sides fought hand-to-hand on the mountaintop for several hours before the Ethiopian army retreated. (Guomin News Agency, 21st)

Northern Italian Army: Consolidating Rear Positions, Outposts Not Advancing Towards Mek'ele 6

Addis Ababa: Since the surrender of Kufsa to the Italian army, telephone communication between Addis Ababa and the northern front has been cut off. It was only restored today. General Seyoum, who is defending against the Italian army in the Aduwa region, reported to the Emperor by telephone that the Italian army has moved its vanguard back and is now consolidating its positions south of the line connecting Axum, Aduwa, and Adigrat. In the past few days, it was widely rumored that the Italian army's outposts were advancing towards the city of Mek'ele, but this has now been proven to be inaccurate. (Reuters, 22nd)

Italian Troops Continuously Departing for East Africa 7

(London) Although diplomatic talks are underway in Rome and Paris to end the Italo-Ethiopian war, the departure of Italian troops from Naples to East Africa has not stopped. Sixteen thousand men left for the front lines at the end of last week. There are still twenty ships in Naples loading troops. The war against Ethiopia is costing Italy a lot of money. According to an announcement by the Italian Ministry of Finance last night, more than 22 million pounds in British gold were spent in the three months before the war alone. (Reuters, 22nd)

British House of Commons Reconvenes: Foreign Secretary Reports on the International Situation, Economic Sanctions Will Not Lead to War, If They Do, All Nations Will Unite to Resist, and Hope "Old Friend" Will Avert Disaster 8

(London) When British Foreign Secretary Hoare began his speech in the House of Commons this afternoon to report on the international situation, he praised the achievements of the late Henderson, Chairman of the Disarmament Conference. He continued, "Problems so urgent, unpleasant, and dangerous as those we face today are unprecedented. British policy has remained unchanged. This is the policy of the British Parliament and the majority of the people of Britain and the Dominions. Outsiders do not understand Britain's sincerity in the new order of international relations and underestimate Britain's efforts to uphold the League of Nations as an impartial instrument of justice. The British government sees the League of Nations as a bridge connecting the United States and Europe. If this bridge is broken, Britain will find cooperation with the European continent difficult and dangerous. The League of Nations has never shown its vibrancy as it does today. We have never used the current dispute as an opportunity to attack Fascism. We have never wanted to interfere in the internal affairs of other countries. We fulfill our responsibilities in Geneva with the sole purpose of upholding the principles of the League Covenant. Some say that economic sanctions against Italy will eventually lead to war. This is a misconception. He believes that if countries collectively implement economic sanctions, the Italo-Ethiopian war will definitely be shortened. Italy would never be so foolish as to attack a single country. If it does, Britain, France, and other members of the League of Nations will unite and resist with full solidarity. Britain has not wanted to take unilateral action since the beginning of the discussions in Geneva. Military sanctions have never been discussed. There is no such plan in British policy. He does not believe that anyone in Europe wants war now. Britain has never proposed to France the consideration of military sanctions against Italy. There is already too much inflammable material in Europe, which is worrying everywhere. He has never taken a biased attitude. Apart from Italy, he was the first to remind the world of the requirements for Italy's development and economic security." The Foreign Secretary concluded by asking, "Is there no way to reach a solution that would make the policy of economic sanctions against an old friend unnecessary?" (Reuters, 22nd)

(London) The House of Commons reconvened at 2:45 PM this afternoon in an atmosphere of excitement. The visitor's gallery was full, and members of the cabinet and opposition leaders were all present. (Reuters, 22nd)

(London) The British Parliament is scheduled to reconvene today, the last meeting before the general election. Many people will participate in the debate when discussing the international situation today. The Foreign Secretary Hoare will speak first, reviewing the developments since the parliament's adjournment in August. Then the new leader of the Labor Party, Attlee, and the leader of the Liberal Party, Samuel, will continue their speeches. The debate will last about three days. Speakers on the government side will include Chancellor of the Exchequer Chamberlain, Lord President of the Council MacDonald, Prime Minister Baldwin, and Minister Eden. The Prime Minister will make a concluding speech on Thursday night. Other important people who will speak include former Foreign Secretary Austen Chamberlain, former Prime Minister George, former Chancellor of the Exchequer Churchill, former First Lord of the Admiralty Amery, former Labor leader Lansbury, and Labor members Cripps and Maxton. The session will only last for four days, with the closing ceremony on the fourth day. (Reuters, 22nd)

Xianghe Villagers Oppose Additional Land Tax, Gather in Crowds Armed to Surround County Government, Bai Jianwu Incites Riot from Within, Authorities Dispatch Personnel to Investigate and Deploy Troops for Prevention 9

(Beiping) Two thousand villagers from four villages in Xianghe County, 100 miles southeast of Pingdong, protested against the county government's additional 30% surcharge on land taxes. On the 20th, they gathered and took up weapons and firearms, marching in groups to petition the county government. On the 21st, they clashed with the county government's defense corps. The county was surrounded, and the county magistrate is still trapped in the city. This morning, the rioters have not yet retreated. After receiving the report, the provincial government has ordered local military police to pay attention to prevention. If the situation escalates further, they will dispatch strong troops to suppress it. Yin Rugeng, commissioner of the Luan-Yu area, visited Shang Zhen this morning after receiving a phone call to inquire about the situation. Because Xianghe County is adjacent to the war zone, he specifically ordered Zhang Qingyu's department of the Second Regiment of the War Zone Security Team to be on strict alert. He also ordered Gao Shimou and Zhang Jianyun, section chiefs of the Jiji-Mi District Office, to go to Xianghe to conduct an on-site investigation. Currently, the rioters are still gathered outside the east gate of the county, and they are in a standoff with the county government's defense corps. More than 20 members of the Japanese Embassy's military police team, led by squad leader Da'an, have been stationed in the city. (Special dispatch, 12th)

(Tianjin) The riot of the people in Xianghe has not yet subsided. The rioters have elected their own county magistrate. On the 22nd, Sun Yuchen's battalion of Li Yun's fifth regiment of the Yanjiao Security Corps was transferred to the vicinity of Xianghe, listening to orders for action. Lieutenant Colonel Tanghxie Guangxiong, staff officer of the Japanese Garrison Army in Tianjin, traveled by car on the 22nd to investigate the truth. It is said that the evil people are being incited by Chinese traitors and others. Zhang Qingyu, commander of the First Regiment of the Security Corps, arrived in Tong County on the 22nd to investigate the incident. Yin Rugeng has telegraphed Chi Molin, acting commissioner of the Jiji-Mi District, to cooperate with the Security Corps and the county magistrate to properly handle the situation. (Special dispatch, 22nd)

(Tianjin) In the Xianghe Civil Disturbance, the rioters elected An Houzhai as county magistrate, publicized the wrongdoings of the former county Public Security Bureau director, and the Public Security Department director was imprisoned in a temple. The rioters issued a declaration. (Dispatch, 22nd)

(Beiping) It has now been determined that the uprising of the Xianghe rebels was orchestrated by Wu Yuting, a former provincial assemblyman who had retired, to gather ignorant people in the name of petitioning and to seize control of county affairs. County Magistrate Zhao Zhongpu has fled. Bai Chunzhi, director of the county Public Security Bureau, and Squad Leader Liu and three others have been taken away by the rebels. The county town is still closed today. The First Regiment of the Special Police has dispatched 150 police officers and is entering Xianghe today to maintain order. The provincial government has sent Wang Runsheng, who arrived in Tongming today, to go to Xianghe to investigate. (Special dispatch, 22nd)

(Beiping) Yesterday, farmers rioted in Xianghe, 40 miles from Beiping, leading a crowd to surround the city. During the riots, one demonstrator flew and injured three people. Today, peace has been declared, and order is being maintained by the defense corps. However, some farmers are still stationed in front of the city gate. Japanese military police rushed from Ping yesterday night to investigate, arresting six plainclothes Japanese hooligans who were involved in the riot, searching them, interrogating them, and then escorting them to Tianjin. (Reuters, 22nd)

Sino-Japanese Wireless Communication: To Be Available in February Next Year, Charge of Fifteen Yuan Per Three Minutes 10

Kwantung Army Plans to Suggest to Russia Resolving Border Disputes, Advocating the Establishment of a Joint Committee 11

(Changchun) It is reported that the "Manchukuo" government, in view of the frequent incidents on the Russian-Manchu border, consulted with the Kwantung Army authorities and will make an important proposal to Soviet Russia. The spokesman did not approve of the shooting being referred to as a border-crossing patrol. He said that if Soviet Russia wants to eliminate the source of such disputes, the Kwantung Army would support the Soviet Russia's proposal to establish a joint committee to resolve the various outstanding issues. However, Soviet Russia always blames Japan or "Manchukuo" for every dispute. This attitude is very frustrating. The Kwantung Army is deeply concerned about protecting the Manchu border, as Japan has the obligation to maintain security within "Manchukuo." (Reuters, 22nd)

Soviet Union October Revolution Anniversary: Preparing for Grand Celebration, Internally Purging Remaining Political Enemies, Externally Fighting Fascism 12

(Moscow) November 7th is the 18th anniversary of the Soviet Union's October Revolution. As usual, a grand celebration will be held. The Central Executive Committee of the Communist Party recently drafted the slogans to be used for this year's October Revolution anniversary. In terms of domestic policy, it focuses on balancing the interests of people in all industries, such as improving the material status of workers, building workers' residences, and increasing nutritious food. In addition, it also pays attention to "purging class enemies and eliminating the remnants of the Zinoviev and Trotsky factions." In terms of foreign policy, it cites the resolutions of the Seventh Congress of the Third International, declaring that "the world is divided into two major camps: aggressive Fascism and peaceful nations." Special tribute is paid to "the French proletariat, who are in the vanguard of anti-Fascism," and "the Ethiopian people, who are engaged in a heroic struggle for national independence." Early December: Naval Conference Convened, British Cabinet Reportedly Decided 17

(London) It is reported that the British Cabinet has decided to convene a preliminary naval conference in London during the first week of December. As Japan has repeatedly demanded absolute equality in naval tonnage, it is considered difficult to reach a significant naval agreement at this time. It is said that when the naval conference convenes, the signatory nations of the Washington and London Naval Treaties will be asked to (1) conclude an agreement whereby signatory nations agree to mutually notify each other in advance of naval shipbuilding programs, and (2) conclude a special agreement to limit the tonnage and gun caliber of various types of warships. It is reported that Japan opposes the first type of agreement but accepts the second. Furthermore, Italy's stance remains unclear. However, since the recent easing of Anglo-Italian diplomatic relations, it is generally believed that negotiations between Britain and Italy on naval issues will proceed more easily. (Havas dispatch on the 21st)

(Japanese Associated Press dispatch on the 22nd)

(Tokyo) The Ministry of Foreign Affairs and the Ministry of the Navy are currently discussing the naval conference that Britain intends to convene in London in December. It is generally believed that Japan will accept this British proposal but with reservations. It is reported that the Ministry of Foreign Affairs has received a telegram from the acting ambassador in London reporting that the British Foreign Office, through Mr. Craigie, has informally notified them of Britain's intention to convene a naval conference in London on December 2nd. British Ambassador Notifies Italy: Britain to Implement Neutrality Law Based on the 1907 Hague Convention 19

(London) In order to limit Italy's commercial relations with various parts of the world, the government today announced the strict implementation of the neutrality law of the 1907 Hague Peace Conference to deal with Italian ships traveling to Britain. On Sunday, the British East Africa government announced the implementation of the neutrality law, forcing Italian ships to depart within 24 hours of arrival. The British government's actions are similar, but are not related to the League of Nations' sanctions. The British Ambassador to Italy, Sir Drummond, personally visited the Italian Ministry of Foreign Affairs today to notify the Italian government of this action. (National News Agency dispatch on the 22nd)

(London) The British Ambassador to Italy, Sir Drummond, met with Italian Prime Minister Mussolini this afternoon and informed him that Britain, its territories, and the Anglo-Egyptian Sudan have decided to implement the neutrality regulations contained in the 1907 Hague Convention. After this notification, Italian ships carrying troops, military supplies, munitions, or water to East Africa will not be allowed to stay in British ports for more than 24 hours, and will only be allowed to purchase some coal and food sufficient to reach another Italian port. It is reported that the Egyptian government has made the same decision. According to London official circles, the implementation of the Hague Neutrality Law is not a sanction against Italy. This law applies to both belligerent nations. However, as Abyssinia does not have ships, only Italy is affected. Italy and Abyssinia have not officially declared war, but Britain believes that a war without a declaration should not receive more favorable treatment than a declared war. Britain has notified the French government of this decision. (Reuters dispatch on the 21st)

Cairo: According to reliable sources, Egypt has not yet decided on the implementation of the neutrality provisions of the 1907 Hague Convention. It is also reported that the Egyptian government does not wish to make a decision on this matter at this time. (Reuters dispatch on the 22nd)

Alexandria: In order to prevent the early implementation of sanctions against Italy, Italy is making every effort to ship 10,000 bales of cotton from here to Italy within this week before the transport ban is issued. Italy previously refused to purchase goods with cash, but in the past few days, cash has been prepared, so Alexandria's exporters, including the Chamber of Commerce, are now loading their cotton onto Italian ships. (Reuters dispatch on the 22nd)

European Gold Continues to Flow to the U.S.

Labour Party Members of the British House of Lords Elect Lord Snell as Leader 22

(London) Labour Party members of the House of Lords gathered in London today and unanimously decided to elect Lord Snell as the leader of the Labour Party in the House of Lords, succeeding Lord Ponsonby. Lord Snell is the Chairman of the London County Council, a member of the Imperial Economic Committee, and a member of the National Labour Party Executive Committee. He studied economics at the University of Nottingham. He began as a rural worker, then worked as a groom and ferryman, later becoming the superintendent of the Nottingham Blind Institute. Soon after, he became the manager of Nottingham charitable organizations. In 1922, he was elected as a Member of Parliament, serving for ten years for the Labour Party. Commentary

How to Prevent Car Accidents 40

— End

Since means of transportation are becoming more novel by the day, accidents caused by reckless driving are frequently heard of. Human life is of utmost importance, and permanent disability is the most painful thing in life. Imagine yourself or your relatives and friends being injured in a car accident, and how much pain and resentment you would feel. Even those who extend benevolence to animals still have practices of protecting life and abstaining from killing. How can human life be treated lightly and trivially? Nowadays, car drivers often blame pedestrians when accidents occur, claiming that they collided with the car because they were not careful when walking. This may be true in some cases, but if drivers can understand the importance of human life, it is not difficult to save people in an instant. Moreover, the dead are gone, who can rise up and ask whether the car killed them or whether they were not careful themselves? If car accidents can be blamed solely on pedestrians, then drivers will become even more careless. Furthermore, killing people and destroying property on sidewalks and blaming it on slippery roads, claiming that it is not the driver's fault, is even more unthinkable.

I have pondered the causes of car accidents: (1) Due to the driver's lack of skill or inadequate physical strength and eyesight. After driving for a long time, they become mentally and physically exhausted and inadvertently cause accidents. Long-distance buses often overturn because drivers do not have the opportunity to rest and recover from fatigue. Some cause accidents because they work day and night without sufficient sleep, indulging in alcohol and pleasure, and losing their ability to drive. (2) Due to mechanical failures, such as brakes losing their effectiveness and drivers being unable to control the vehicle freely. (3) Those who ride in cars are usually wealthy and influential, and are not afraid of fines, which they do not value. As a result, drivers dare to disregard everything. (4) A few individuals who rely on special influence and are not subject to our laws often drive at high speeds and arbitrarily violate traffic regulations. (5) Commercial vehicles sometimes disregard traffic regulations, driving at high speeds to compete for passengers, often leading to jealousy, fights, car damage, and injuries. These are generally the causes of accidents.

We believe that in order to ensure the safety of the public on the roads: (1) The granting of driver's licenses should be subject to strict examination, and vehicles should be inspected at any time to verify the condition of their machinery. (2) Traffic regulations should be strictly enforced without any preferential treatment based on the driver's status. As the American court did not lightly forgive President Roosevelt's son for violating traffic regulations, this is commendable. (3) In addition to revoking driver's licenses, causing death should not be limited to fines, but should also be subject to imprisonment. Only in this way will money be ineffective and people will know what to fear. (4) Those who are recklessly disregardful should be dealt with by the local authorities through negotiation to supplement the shortcomings of the law. (5) Shanghai's roads were originally only for horse-drawn carriages and pedestrians. In the past twenty years, the city's commerce has flourished and automobiles have developed. The old roads are insufficient to accommodate them. Especially in the city, the roads still retain their old-style streets and alleys. Rickshaws must yield to each other, but automobiles are also allowed to pass at the same time, causing great distress to pedestrians. Therefore, the danger of traffic accidents cannot be reduced without reorganizing the roads as soon as possible. This is what we hope from the municipal authorities.

Representatives from Three Provinces Hold First Boundary Survey Meeting in Xunyang, Depart Tomorrow to Survey, Expected to Finish in One Week 41

(Jiujiang) The representatives from Henan Province and representatives from the Provinces of Hubei, Jiangxi and Anhui, a total of ten people including Zhang Xun, held their first meeting on the afternoon of the 22nd to survey the provincial boundary of Hunan. It was decided that on the morning of the 24th, they will take a small steamboat to the junction of Hubei and Jiangxi and then to the junction of Anhui and Jiangxi to survey the intertwined boundary line of the three provinces in northern Hunan, from Baihua Dike to Tongren Dike, about 200 kilometers long. This survey is expected to be completed in one week. As for the demarcation method, one representative from Hunan stated that they will exchange opinions after the survey. (Central News Agency dispatch on the 22nd)

Details of the Measures for Distributing and Supplementing Personnel Recruited with Lenience in the Higher Civil Service Examination

(Nanjing) The Ministry of Personnel is now drafting two measures for distributing and supplementing personnel recruited with lenience in the Higher Civil Service Examination. The distribution of personnel recruited with lenience in the Ordinary Civil Service Examination will also be handled in accordance with these measures. The measures have been submitted to the National Government for approval and are as follows: (1) Those who have been recruited with lenience in accordance with the law and have experience of serving in a commissioned position for more than two years may be exempted from training when assigned to serve in border provinces. When assigned to serve in non-border provinces, they should undergo one year of training. (2) Those who do not have the experience of serving in a commissioned position as mentioned above, or whose experience is less than two years, should undergo one year of training when assigned to serve in border provinces. When assigned to serve in non-border provinces, they should undergo two years of training. (Central News Agency dispatch from the 22nd)

Resolution of Shantou Smuggling Incident

The Agreement was Signed at Noon on the 16th, and the Japanese Warship Left Shantou on the Evening of the 17th, but the Contents Were Not Announced.

A correspondence from Shantou reports that the detention of smuggled rice, oil, and soybeans in Jieyang has been a serious situation since September 10. The Japanese Navy dispatched Rear Admiral Masasuke Shimomura, commander of the 5th Torpedo Squadron, leading the Ryuta, Fujino, Asagao, Karukaya, Tadeo, Fuji, and Ren ships, claiming to protect Japanese residents and declaring that they would not leave Shantou until a satisfactory solution was reached. This caused great anxiety among the citizens. Furthermore, the Japanese Marine Corps repeatedly landed in groups, parading on the streets, gathering at the Toyo School, or at the train station, which led to the constant spread of strange rumors. The Guangzhou authorities sent Wu Bosheng to Shantou to handle the negotiations. However, both sides maintained secrecy, making it difficult to know the specific details. It is rumored that the Japanese side put forward the following conditions: (1) Japanese merchants transporting goods such as oil, soybeans, rice, sugar, foreign yarn, seafood, matches, and tobacco essence will be exempted from all local special taxes, miscellaneous taxes, and surcharges in addition to paying regular customs duties when transporting them into Shantou and the Chaozhou-Meizhou hinterland; (2) In order to prevent accidental harassment or obstruction of Japanese and Taiwanese merchants operating and transporting goods, a commercial district will be designated from Youtouqi to Xinxing Road, and docks and warehouses will be built at the end of Shenzhao Road, and commercial commissioners and warehouses will be established in prosperous fair markets in the Chaozhou and Jieyang hinterland to facilitate the sale of goods in the local area. The oil, rice, and soybeans detained in Jieyang must be returned and losses compensated; (3) The government must issue a proclamation protecting trade, canceling previous secret orders issued by the military and local groups to assist in the seizure of smuggled goods. Local officials must assist Japanese merchants in building docks in Qilu and prevent various northern groups or the public from obstructing in the name of opposition; (4) The government should be responsible for protecting Japanese merchants' goods transported to the hinterland for sale and not allow the people to use the name of any group to repel or obstruct them; (5) Guarantee that there will be no recurrence of similar incidents; (6) The Japanese side will build an air force landing field in Shantou to facilitate civilian flights from Taiwan to Shantou. The above six items are what the Japanese and Taiwanese people in Shantou have said. The Cantonese province was given until the 14th to respond. The government side refused to make a public announcement and strictly prohibited the dissemination of the above information. However, based on reason and theory, the Japanese side's requests, such as releasing the detained rice, compensating for losses, and Japanese merchants' goods being exempted from all other local taxes other than customs duties, and that the tax inspection and local military police should not obstruct Japanese merchants transporting goods to the hinterland, are more credible. Other items are likely to be deliberately released by the Japanese and Taiwanese to create an atmosphere. After Wu Bosheng arrived in Shantou, he collaborated with Mayor Li Yuanhe and Customs Superintendent Zhang Jinghui to take charge of the negotiations. At the same time, Fan Zhanpeng, the deputy director of anti-smuggling, also increased the number of anti-smuggling soldiers in Shantou. Li Hanhun requested Guangzhou to send more military police to Shantou to maintain order and reassure the people. According to reports, by the 11th, the Shantou Municipal Government had sent Secretary Li Chaofan and Fan Zhanpeng back to the province to report. At the same time, Gan Jiehou also negotiated with Japanese Consul General Kawa Tatsuo stationed in Guangzhou. On the 16th, both parties had already agreed that each other considered it a local incident. At 11:00 a.m. that day, Shantou Mayor Li Yuanhe, according to instructions from the province, immediately signed a resolution with Japanese Consul General Harada Tadaichi in a satisfactory atmosphere. Rear Admiral Masasuke Shimomura, commander of the Japanese fleet, also visited Li Hanhun at the Eastern District Pacification Commissioner's Office. In the evening, Li Yuanhe hosted a banquet at the Police Recreation Association to entertain Shimomura, Harada, and others, with Customs Superintendent Zhang Jinghui and many others accompanying them. On the 17th, Li Hanhun returned the visit to the Japanese consulate, and Li Yuanhe also returned the visit to Shimomura on the Ryuta ship. At about 6:00 p.m., two Japanese warships left Shantou in the dim twilight, but one Japanese warship remained in the port of Shantou and had not left. (18th)

Implementation of Extraterritorial Communication

Chinese and English Telegrams Opened on the 16th, Japanese Telegrams Starting on November 1st

A correspondence from Tianjin reports that Wang Ruoxi, Director of the Tianjin Telegraph Bureau, Yin Tong, Director of the Beining Railway Bureau, Takeshita Yoshiharu, Chief of the Kwantung Army's Special Service Agency in Shanhaiguan, and Fujiwara Yasuaki, Director of the Manchurian Postal Service, began to discuss the issue of extraterritorial communication in June of this year. After more than ten meetings in Beidaihe, Beiping, and Tianjin, they finally decided on the general outline of all communication and signed an agreement on the 30th of last month. Except for the sending and receiving of Japanese telegrams, which will be handled starting on November 1st due to the time required for preparation, the Chinese and English plain and cipher telegrams will be handled starting on October 16th. This matter was already implemented informally in the spring of this year. The only difference is how to settle the telegram fees, and that Japanese telegrams are still not sent or received. This agreement is a contractual agreement on the previously implemented items to be observed by both parties. Previously, the telegram fees were collected and used independently. Now, according to international communication practice, the sending and receiving bureaus keep daily accounts and settle them once at the end of each month. However, neither party directly assumes responsibility for the settlement. The Huito Transfer Company, the organizer of postal services in Shanhaiguan, is entrusted with the matter. Surpluses are paid, and deficits are supplemented. The domestic communication bureaus are limited to the telegraph bureaus in Tianjin and Beiping. Extraterritorially, they are limited to the Kwantung Prefecture area, the railway affiliated area along the South Manchuria Railway, and Shenyang, Jilin, Changchun, Harbin, and Qiqihar. The remaining branch bureaus in various places do not send or receive telegrams. If telegrams are sent to places other than the above sending and receiving bureaus, the receiving bureaus will forward them themselves after receiving them. In addition to English and Chinese, telegrams in Japanese are also sent and received. The fee for ordinary Chinese telegrams is 12 cents per word for plain text and 24 cents per word for cipher text. The name and address of the recipient are also charged at the rate of two words. English telegrams are sent and received according to the international communication fee calculation method. For Japanese telegrams, every five Japanese letters are counted as a sentence, and the fee is the same as the Chinese example. The fee for news telegrams is reduced by a quarter, and the fee for urgent telegrams is doubled. The Tianjin Telegraph Bureau, in order to handle Japanese telegrams immediately, specially requested permission from the Ministry of Communications to transfer eight Japanese telegram operators from the Qingdao Telegraph Bureau to Tianjin to assist. On November 1st, only Japanese telegrams can be received first. Due to machine issues, outbound telegrams are scheduled to be implemented on January 1st of next year. Wang Ruoxi, Director of the Tianjin Telegraph Bureau, is responsible for handling this matter. On the 19th, he was summoned to Beijing by telegram by the Ministry of Communications to present everything. After the 918 Incident, when the Northeast was lost, communication outside the customs never ceased. Inbound and outbound telegrams were connected through the Tianjin Radio Station and the Harbin Radio Station. Foreigners in China, except for political and military news, could still transmit them. Now that an agreement has been clearly concluded, it should be much more convenient than before. (20th)

The Beginning and End of the Bandit Remnants' Escape to Gansu

The Bandit Leaders Have Conflicting Opinions, and the Bandit Masses are Also Surrendering One After Another

A correspondence from Lanzhou reports that after the Zhu, Mao, Xu, and Peng bandits joined forces in western Sichuan, they suffered almost complete losses in strength due to the encirclement and suppression by the National Army. Furthermore, because the northwestern region is located on a plateau with perennial snow cover and is extremely barren, making it impossible to survive, they had to find another way out. Therefore, they had the intention of fleeing north. In early September, they attempted to flee to Qinghai. However, because the southern part of Qinghai is mostly barren, and miasma occurs from time to time, not only was there no food, but even drinking water was a problem. Furthermore, they were attacked by Tibetan soldiers. Their cunning plan failed, and the bandit leaders held a meeting in Mao'ergai to decide on future actions. At that time, there were different opinions, and they blamed each other. Zhu and Mao blamed Xu and Chen for the failure to cross the Jialing River, and Xu and Chen blamed Zhu and Mao for the long-term fighting in Jiangxi, which led to the loss of strength. In the end, it was decided that Zhu and Zhang would lead the pseudo-59th and 2nd Army Corps and the pseudo-9th and 31st Army to flee north across the Yellow River via Heba, and Xu and Zhou would lead the pseudo-1st and 3rd Army Corps and the pseudo-4th and 30th Army to flee north via Baozuo. It was unexpected that the opinions of the people in the valley had long been inconsistent. Therefore, the pseudo-chiefs of the Baozuo clan soon held a meeting, and Mao advocated fleeing to Gansu, while Xu and Chen advocated returning to Li Mao. The meeting ended without a conclusion. The next morning, Mao, Peng, and others arbitrarily led the pseudo-1st and 3rd Army Corps to flee north towards Minxia, and Xu also led the pseudo-4th and 30th Army to flee back to Mao'ergai. Zhu was still near Awa.

The bandits who fled to Gansu were the main forces of Mao Zedong, Lin Biao, Peng Dehuai, and others, initially numbering about 10,000 people. They fled towards Min County and came into contact with the Lu division of the National Army several times. Due to the disparity in numbers, they were unable to repel the bandits. Later, the Tang Huaiyuan unit of the 12th Division of the National Army arrived in Min County in a timely manner and gave the bandits a head-on blow, causing them to suffer heavy losses. Failing to capture Min County, they turned east and fled. The 5th Cavalry Regiment of the National Army pursued the bandits, who fled to Tongwei through Hadapu, Qingjiayi, Xinshizhen, Yuanyangpu and other places. When they reached Tongwei, the county seat was occupied because there were no garrison troops. The county seat was soon recovered by the Mao Bingwen unit of the National Army, and Mao immediately pursued the bandits relentlessly, day and night. After the bandits were defeated in Tongwei, they fled to Jieshipu, Qingjiayi, Jiangjunbao, and Zhang Yibao, suffering repeated heavy losses along the way. Coupled with the lack of food and long marches, they were exhausted. More than half of them were killed or wounded, and countless surrendered to the National Army on their own initiative. After the remnant bandits passed the Liupan Mountains, they were blocked by the He cavalry and the 35th Division of the National Army stationed in eastern Gansu. Currently, there are less than 2,000 people left. The National Army has pursued them to the Hongde City area of Huai County. With a large army blocking them in front and a heroic division pursuing them relentlessly behind, the annihilation of the bandits is not far off.

The remaining bandits in Sichuan, without food or clothing, and suffering from miasma and epidemics, wanted to flee north, but were blocked by a large army and could not cross Leichi for a single step. According to recent news, bandits are dying from starvation, cold, and the spread of epidemics. It is estimated that more than 10,000 have died in the past month. Furthermore, winter is approaching, and it will be even more difficult for the remnants to survive. (October 18)

The Water Patrol Continues to Capture Bandits

Robberies have been frequent in the Peinan area recently. The case of a truck being robbed by bandits on the Shanghai-Hangzhou Highway in Yanggongmiao caused a stir. Jiang Zhenglin then confessed that a fellow accomplice named Xia Zhengyu. He has now been arrested at Xia's hideout and is currently being interrogated at the team headquarters in the hope of capturing all the criminals in one fell swoop.

Silk Factories Increase Wages

The Wuxi Silk Factory Industry Union Organizing Committee convened the organizers of various factory branches on the 22nd to hold the first representative meeting. Tao Shensheng chaired the meeting and resolved: (1) The working hours of each factory should be communicated to the Silk Factory Association by letter, and the factories should be required to strictly implement the "six in, six out" rule; (2) Increase workers' wages as the silk market soars; (3) Restore silkworm moth subsidies; (4) Worker bonuses should be set at two working days per month; (5) Workers' wages should be paid no later than the 16th of the following month to maintain workers' livelihoods.

Yangzhou

The County Government Prohibits the Smuggling of Grain for Export

Since the autumn grain harvest in this county, rice prices have increased instead of decreasing. It is learned that the increase in the price of rice has continued to increase in recent times, and the poor people who generally seek to make a living are all suffering because of this. However, there are different opinions on the reasons for the high price. Some say that it is due to unscrupulous merchants smuggling exports, and others say that wealthy people in various villages are hoarding and speculating. It is heard that the county government, in view of the fact that the city is in poverty and the yellow peril is inevitable in Yangzhou, how can it allow rice prices to continue to soar? It is proposed to issue a strict ban on the export of food without a permit, and to crack down on hoarding and speculation in rural households in order to maintain the people's food supply.

London Gold Price Today is 141 Shillings and 7 Pence, Up 2 Pence. International Commercial Telegraph, October 22, Reuters Special Business Report

Gold and Silver

British Silver: The London silver market is stable, spot prices unchanged, at 29 3/125 pence. Futures fell 0.06125 to 29.25 pence. India and China sold, and the United States bought.

Exchange Rates

British/American: The foreign exchange market in London is dull today, with no major changes. The opening exchange rate between British and American currencies was 4 yuan, 9 jiao, 1 fen, 3/125, which was 0.0625 lower than yesterday's British/American closing price. At noon, it fell 1/125 to 4 yuan, 9 jiao, 1 fen, 1/875, and there were no further changes.

British/French: The opening price rose by 3 pounds, to 74 francs, 53. After an hour, it fell by 2 pounds, to 74 francs, 51, with no further changes.

Cotton and Wheat

American Cotton: Although there is not much demand from the industry, overseas telegrams are good. Therefore, the opening price of the New York cotton market rose this morning, and then turned dull because operators obviously wanted to wait until the hedging sales eased before purchasing.

British Cotton: The Liverpool cotton market also fell slightly. At 1:00 p.m., the price for January futures was 6.03, down 2 pounds.

British Wheat: The Liverpool wheat market has turned positive today due to the improvement in the international situation. At 1:00 p.m., the price for December futures was 6 shillings, 4 pence, 25, down 0.875.

American Wheat: The Chicago wheat market was affected by the sharp drop in Liverpool wheat prices. Therefore, the opening price fell by 0.0625. The market situation was loose, and prices were even lower due to hedging sales. The opening price of coarse grains was unchanged. Later, due to the replenishment of the missing parties, the price rose slightly.

Rubber

London: The London rubber market was quiet this morning. The opening transaction price for January and March futures was 6 pence, 4375, the same as yesterday's closing price. There was no change at noon.

New York: The opening price of rubber fell by 0.07 pounds, mostly due to sales by brokers. Although the market situation was still loose when the telegram was sent, the price did not continue to change.

Securities

New York: The New York securities market was firm this morning, except for mining and railway stocks. However, railway stocks also turned firm later. The market situation was stable for a while, and then gradually became uneven because those who profited from the liquidation rose one after another. The Two Railway Bureaus Held a Joint Land, Sea, and Air Transportation Conference Yesterday

More Than 10 Representatives from the Ministry of Railways Attended

The Conference Will Continue This Afternoon and Today

The Shanghai-Nanjing and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railways, in order to improve joint transportation facilities and increase convenience for passengers and merchants, invited a joint transportation conference, which was held at 9:30 a.m. yesterday in the conference room of the Traffic Department of the railway. Those attending included Yang Songqing, Deputy Director of the Joint Transportation Department of the Ministry of Railways, 21 representatives from land, sea, and air transportation agencies along the route (representing 15 units), Huang Boqiao, Director of the Railway Bureau, Wu Shaozeng, Deputy Director, and other designated attendees and observers. They were all invited to the venue. Director Huang chaired the meeting. After the ceremony, the chairman stood up to introduce the representatives of the Ministry of Railways, Director Yang, and the representatives from all parties to each other, and the meeting began. Director Yang, Director Huang, and Xiao Weiguo of the Traffic Department gave speeches successively. At noon, a banquet was held at the New Asia Hotel. The meeting continued at 2 p.m. to discuss proposals. The details are recorded below:

Names of Attendees:

Sun Chenchu and Zhu Xinshan of Xicheng Long-Distance Bus Company; Lu Shao Liu and Zhu Ganchen of Zhendao Long-Distance Bus Company; Jiang Huichan and Guo Songru of Zhendanjinbiao Long-Distance Bus Company; Bai Minshi and Xu Housen of Anhui Jingwuxi Section Long-Distance Bus Company; Wang Jizhang of Shanghai-Taicang Long-Distance Bus Company; Lou Zhi of Shaochengshan Bus Company; Xie Xianglin and Zhang Dexi of Fanyao Long-Distance Bus Company; Wang Bangtao and Li Lingzhi of Zhejiang Provincial Highway Administration; Jin Tanghou of Songxin Road Automobile Co., Ltd.; Xi Pengnian of Zhuan Steamboat Company; Jie Guanwu of Jiading Shipping Company; Lu Zhiyu and Shi Shouqi of China Merchants Inland Steamboat Company; Tao Gongliang of Taixing Steamboat Company; Fang Shou Zhang and Wang Tingchen of Tongshang Steamboat Bureau; Xia Sumin and Xia Zhegong of Tongda Yuanji Steamboat Bureau; Sun Yingu and Dong Yizhi of XinYun Joint Transportation Company; Huang Baoxian and He Zhijing of China Aviation Company; Zheng Hongyan and Pan Guangyu of China Travel Service; and Huang Boqiao, Director of the Two Railway Bureaus, Wu Shaozeng, Deputy Director, and the heads of various departments and sections.

Speech by Representative of the Ministry of Railways

Yang Songqing, Representative of the Ministry of Railways, said in his speech that the main expression of the railway business is the transportation business. The development of the transportation business directly increases the income of the railway and indirectly benefits the national economy and the people's livelihood. Because of the convenience of transportation, goods can flow smoothly, which can increase production on the one hand and develop the economy on the other. Our country is in the midst of national difficulties, facing the oppression of the world economy externally and feeling the panic of rural decline internally. In the future, the railway policy will take the vigorous development of transportation as the first priority to reverse the economic panic, and joint transportation is of great importance. If the joint transportation business is not completed in one day, it will be difficult for transportation to reach the extreme point of convenience and speed. In the past three years, we have realized that the development of transportation and joint transportation business cannot be delayed. Therefore, we held responsible transportation in the 21st year and restored the national railway cargo responsible joint transportation in the 22nd year. Although it has been successful step by step, we cannot think that it has reached the realm of success. It can only be regarded as the initial start of the work. Although the joint transportation between railways has been successful, the joint transportation between railways and land, sea, and air is still in its early stages. The further connection and development is the only goal of our future efforts, and it is the mission that all of you present here should jointly shoulder. The Shanghai-Nanjing and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railways are located in a strategic location, and all the areas along the route are prosperous and fertile lands in the southeast. Waterways and highways are scattered like stars and as dense as spider webs. All the various land, sea, and air transportation agencies are as dependent on the Shanghai-Nanjing and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railways as the auxiliary vehicles, and it is necessary to seek mutual connection

The Broker is Dazzled by Lime and Loses His Eyesight; Handgun Snatched

Around 4 AM yesterday, at the entrance of Shoupin Lane on Huade Road in eastern Shanghai, while the neighborhood watchman, who guarded Number 1618 of the lane, was on night watch, four thugs wearing short blue cotton shirts and trousers suddenly appeared. Wu Kunlin Attempts Suicide Twice, Survives

Once Saved from Jumping Off a Building by a Friend, Again Rescued from Drowning by Boatmen

—The Reason for Suicide is Utterly Worthless—

At 11 PM on the 20th of this month, a young man attempted to jump from the fourth floor of the Great World amusement arcade near the New West Bridge in the French Concession. Fortunately, he was pulled back by a friend at the critical moment, averting a tragedy. As it was nearly midnight, many tourists were gathered at the arcade, so word of the incident quickly spread. Showing his determination to die, the same man jumped into the Suzhou River from the Zhashan Road Bridge around 1 PM yesterday. As it was daytime, his actions alarmed many boatmen, who cried for help and rescued him. He was then taken to the police station. During interrogation, he identified himself as Wu Kunlin, 14 years old, from Jiujiang, residing at Number 55 Jianzhong Lane, Avenue Joffre, French Concession. His family lives in the countryside. He used to work as a shop assistant for a Westerner across the street, but the Westerner has returned to his country, leaving Wu Kunlin unemployed for three years. As his family in his hometown is relatively well-off, he has not experienced financial difficulties. However, the reason for his suicide is quite laughable. He claimed that after arguing with his brother, he was determined to wander in Shanghai and vowed never to return home. Now, because his family in the countryside has cut off financial support, he is facing economic pressure but still refuses to return home. As a result, he has exhausted all his resources and seeks death as a solution. The police officers, upon hearing this, criticized him for his actions being utterly worthless. They then found three suicide notes on his person. One was addressed to his parents, vaguely stating that he had repeatedly received instructions to return home, which he dared not disobey. However, he found it difficult to make a living in Shanghai, and returning home in such a state would be a disgrace to his family, and that his wife could remarry. Another was addressed to his uncle and aunt, vaguely stating that he was forced to commit suicide by jumping off a building due to livelihood issues in Shanghai, without any other intentions. The last was a personal account filled with complaints, which was omitted. The police station, concerned that he might attempt suicide again, ordered detective Huang Songsheng to summon his friend to take him home and keep a close watch on him, sending him back to his hometown.

French Concession Orders Residents to Provide Their Own Garbage Bins

Garbage to be Cleared by Laborers Hired by the Municipal Council at Specific Times

The French Concession Municipal Council has established specific measures for clearing garbage within the Concession and has issued a notice for residents to comply. The original text states: "Notice: All residents within the French Concession must comply with the following garbage regulations. Each household should provide its own convenient, covered garbage bin inside its main or secondary building for disposing of daily household garbage. The Municipal Council has a model garbage bin for sale, which residents can purchase. Unless otherwise agreed upon by the Municipal Council and property owners, laborers hired by the Municipal Council to transport garbage are not allowed to enter private residences, private roads, or alleyways. Residents should place the garbage bin next to the road each morning when the garbage truck passes. The garbage inside the bin will be cleared by the Municipal Council's laborers. It is forbidden to place garbage on public roads, open spaces, or in ditches. The garbage bin should not be placed at the roadside before the garbage truck arrives, nor should it be left on the roadside after the garbage truck has passed. The Municipal Council may, upon the request of landlords, clean garbage in private roads and alleyways, but the landlord must prepay a handling fee equal to 4% of the total monthly rental income of all properties in that area every six months. Garbage truck passage times are as follows: April 1st to September 30th, 5 AM to 8 AM; October 1st to March 31st of the following year, 6 AM to 9 AM. Each garbage truck will have a bell that rings when it passes to alert residents. Violations of these regulations will be fined between one and five dollars, and repeat offenders will be subject to double penalties. (Note:) Garbage refers to kitchen waste and household dust. Garden waste, animal waste, or bricks and soil should not be considered garbage and should be disposed of by the residents themselves. The Municipal Council hereby reminds residents of the French Concession that disposing of garbage on the roadside will have many adverse effects (such as breeding flies and propagating harmful bacteria). Therefore, all residents within the Concession are urged to comply with these regulations in good faith."

Western Shanghai Farmer, A Long, Experiences Robbery on His Wedding Night

Father Beaten on the Head

Silverware Stolen

Tang Junpei, a farmer from Guangang Township in western Shanghai, is over sixty years old. His son, A Long, is thirty years old and works as a carpenter in Shanghai. He was not yet married. This spring, a colleague, Mr. Wang from Pu, acted as a matchmaker, arranging a marriage with Miss Ding from Chongming Island. The wedding was held on the 18th of this month. However, around 10 PM the night before yesterday, several robbers broke into the house and rushed into the bridal chamber. The newlyweds woke up in shock and cried for help. The robbers used guns to prevent them from making noise. They dragged the groom out of bed, flirted with the bride, snatched two gold rings from her hand, smashed open a suitcase, and stole over ten dollars and a leather cheongsam. They then beat A Long and forced him to hand over silver dollars. A Long pleaded that he had borrowed money from relatives and friends for the wedding and still owed money for the banquet, so he had no silver dollars. The robbers then stole a silk robe and a watch. As the robbers were leaving, A Long's father cried for help and was beaten on the head with a stick. He sought medical attention at Shanghai Hospital yesterday. Fortunately, his life is not in danger. However, A Long, newly married, has suffered this tragedy and is deeply traumatized.

Dispute at Yixin Toothbrush Factory Resolved Through Mediation by the General Labor Union

Two Resolutions Reached by Both Parties

The Yixin Toothbrush Factory on Xietu Road in the South City recently announced that it would cancel the no-work subsidy and provide only a 20-cent meal allowance starting on August 1 due to the impact of the sluggish market, which aroused opposition from all workers. The Toothbrush Workers' Union sent representatives to negotiate with the factory several times, but no results were achieved. The Municipal General Labor Union believed that if the case was not resolved, it would inevitably lead to unexpected disputes, so it specially invited both parties to mediate at 2 PM yesterday. Manager Dai from the factory and Zhao Fayuan and others from the workers' side attended. After repeated persuasion, two resolutions were reached: (1) The no-work subsidy will be changed to 45 cents (7.5 cents per hour) from October 1, 1935. This measure will be valid for one year. If the factory's business does not improve after one year, it may continue to be effective. Both parties were satisfied and declared the resolution.

Daxin Hotel, founded by business magnate Mr. Ge Pinsheng, is located at the intersection of Guangxi Road and Ningbo Road and will officially open today. The location is central and convenient, the interior is beautifully decorated, the layout is modern, the rooms are clean, the air is fresh, and the facilities are perfect. All rooms, large and small, are equipped with washbasins, hot and cold water taps, and shared bathrooms that are open day and night. Free cards are provided for entertainment. Rooms start from 60 cents, and bathroom rooms start from 1.60 yuan. It is said that those who have booked rooms have praised it unanimously.

Zhang Guoqing and Others Use Cruel Methods

Administering Criminal Tattoo to Thief

Tattooing the Words "Robber" on the Thief's Face with Blue Ink

According to forensic medical appraisal, these two words can no longer be erased.

Teng Shunzi from Yangzhou broke into Zhang Guoqing's house at No. 46 Lane 36, Tianbao Road, Zhabei on the night of September 21 to commit theft. He was caught on the spot by Zhang Guoqing, who, together with Wang Dacheng, Wang Maojun, and others, tied Teng Shunzi to a pillar, beat him, and used a needle to tattoo the words "Robber" on Teng's left cheek, applying blue ink. Then, they released him. Teng Shunzi suffered a lifelong humiliation and reported the incident to the local police, who arrested Zhang Guoqing, Wang Dacheng, and Wang Maojun and took them to the police station together with Teng Shunzi. The case was forwarded to the Procuratorate of the District Court, where Prosecutor Zhang Zi determined that Teng Shunzi had committed the crime of Article 321, Paragraph 1 and 2 of the Criminal Law, and Zhang Guoqing, Wang Dacheng, Wang Maojun, and others had committed the crime of Article 278, Paragraph 1 of the same law. Yesterday morning at 10:00 AM, Judge Wu Xiangzu specially opened the 13th court to hear the case. After the judge took his seat, he ordered the detention of Teng Shunzi, Zhang Guoqing, Wang Dacheng, Wang Maojun, and others to the court. First, Teng Shunzi testified that he was 25 years old and had been forced by unemployment and hunger to commit theft. Unfortunately, he was caught by them, who first beat him severely and then tied him to a pillar and stabbed him with a long needle on his left face, causing unbearable pain. Even if he begged along the streets, no one would give him money because of the words on his face. Therefore, he reported the incident to the police, requesting justice. As he finished his testimony, he looked up and asked the court to examine the obvious "Robber" words on his face (about the size of copper coins). Then, Zhang Guoqing testified that he was 23 years old, from Yangzhou, and worked to make a living. Teng Shunzi came to steal, and he caught him, but he did not beat or tattoo him. Wang Maojun testified that he was 21 years old, from Taixing. Wang Dacheng testified that he was 21 years old, from Taixing. Their testimonies were generally the same as Zhang Guoqing's. The judge, upon hearing the testimonies, said, "Are you imitating the ancients in treating those who tunnel and steal by tattooing their faces for identification, so that people can see them and take precautions?" Zhang and others replied together, "We did not tattoo him." The judge said, "He committed theft, and you should have reported it to the police and arrested him. How could you use such cruel methods, making it impossible for him to stand in society? According to forensic medical appraisal, the tattoo cannot be erased. Your actions are too cruel. The crime you committed is punishable by five to twelve years. You should confess the truth. Who came up with the idea, and who tattooed him?" However, Zhang Guoqing and others denied it and tried to deny it. At this point, Prosecutor Zhang came to the court and stated his opinion. The judge concluded that the case was clear and decided to end it. The verdict will be announced at 10:00 AM on the 29th of this month. All defendants were returned to custody.

Investigating and Punishing Those Who Assaulted Volleyball Referees During the National Games

The first meeting of the third board of directors of the National Sports Advancement Association was held on October 19th at the New Asia Hotel in Shanghai. The attendees were Zhang Boling, Wang Zhengting, Hao Gengsheng, Shen Siliang, Chu Minyi, Wu Yunrui, Ma John, Yuan Dunli, Wu Tiecheng, Wang Zhuoran, Dong Shouyi, and Gao Zi. The absentees were Song Junfu, Zhu Jiahua, and Zhang Jiwu. The meeting began at 7 PM, and Zhang Boling was elected as the temporary chairman. The resolutions were as follows:

Nomination of Executive Honorary Directors

(1) Wang Zhengqian was elected as the chairman of the board of directors.

(2) Four executive directors were elected: Chu Minyi, Hao Gengsheng, Shen Siliang, and Wu Yunrui.

(3) Shen Siliang was appointed as honorary secretary-general.

(4) The position of honorary president was abolished.

(5) Six honorary directors were appointed: Jin Zengcheng, Hu Wenhu, Li Qingquan, Shang Zhen, Shen Honglie, and Chen Shi.

(6) The list of members for each committee will be determined and appointed by the executive board.

Appointing Committee Members to Organize Regional Branches

(7) The members of the association will be reorganized based on region (starting in 1937). The method for the election of the next board of directors should be that each region appoints one person, and the rest are elected by the representative assembly.

(8) For those regional branches that have not been properly organized, committee members will be appointed to be responsible for convening and organizing them.

Cheng Dengke, Zhang Deshan, Liu Shenzhi, Huang Cishu, Ma Zezhao, Yang Xiaozhai, and Wu Shengwu are appointed as committee members to prepare for the organization of the Northwest Sports Advancement Association.

Wu Demao, Xu Minhui, and Lu Qihua are appointed as committee members to prepare for the organization of the South China Regional Branch. Wu Bangwei, Wu Yunrui, Chen Baiqing, and Shen Siliang are appointed as committee members to prepare for the organization of the East China Regional Branch. The committee members for Central China will be investigated and appointed.

Investigating the Assailant Players During the National Games

(9) Investigate the qualifications of the athletes in this National Games, and then warn the unit to which the assailant belongs.

The Central China Sports Association Established in Shanghai

The Central China Sports Association was initiated three years ago and has been in preparation for a considerable time. Taking advantage of the opportunity of the 6th National Games being held in Shanghai, and with the representatives and general team leaders of the four provinces of Hunan, Hubei, Jiangxi, and Anhui all in Shanghai, the inaugural meeting was held the day before yesterday at the Municipal Central Stadium. Huang Fengqi, the representative of Hunan, presided over the meeting. The attendees included Zeng Fusheng from Hunan, Song Ruhai, Chen Shi, Liu Changhe, He Jianping, Deng Kanshun from Hubei, Luo Liangzhu, Wu Zhongjun, Wu Yunlong from Anhui. After three hours of discussion, the charter was approved, and executive committee members were elected. Those elected were Zhu Jingnong, Fang Kegang, Huang Fengqi from Hunan, Cheng Qibao, Chen Ye, Liu Changhe from Hubei, Cheng Qiyuan, Yu Yongzuo, Deng Kanshun from Jiangxi, Yang Liankui, Dan Hua, and Wu Zhongjun from Anhui. Subsequently, Fang, Liu, and Yu were mutually elected as standing committee members, and Song Ruhai was appointed as the secretary-general. The association's headquarters will be located in Zhongshan Park, Hankou, and it was also decided that the next Central China Games will be held in Changsha.
