Free Talk: New Autumn Scenery of the Japanese Literary World (Tokyo Correspondence) by Luo Zhi

A Japanese writer said in a literary review that the phenomenon in the Japanese literary world is like a couple quarreling in the middle of the night, with only sharp cries and shouts, and no way to know the inside story. Although this remark has a bit of humor, it also has some truth. For example, the "New Social School," "New Psychological School," and "New Sensationalist School" of a few years ago can be included in this kind of example. Even recently, isn't this kind of metabolism still being played out? Regarding this, we can cite "Activism," "Verbatim Literature," and "Accidentalism."

The Defeat of Activism

The so-called activism in Japan is essentially a combination of Japanese liberalism and the French "humanism of action." Ten years ago, liberalism and leftist thought could be said to be the two major ideological trends standing side by side in Japan. The former originated in France, while the latter originated in Russia and Germany. Later, leftist thought gained momentum and suppressed liberalism. This continued until last year when leftist thought suffered a temporary setback. At the same time, liberalism was revived by the new convergence of the French "humanism of action." As a result, the magazine "Action" was founded as a publication platform, and a series of books were published, which indeed had the potential to sweep the entire Japanese literary world. However, by April and May of this year, signs of decline had already appeared. At that time, Komatsu Kiyoshi, a theorist of activism, made such a bold statement in order to save the situation: "If no one else will do it, I will do it alone!" In this way, he barely managed to support it until now, but finally, he could no longer support it, and he had to announce the suspension of publication of its organ, "Action." Now, looking back on the gains of activism, what are they? Perhaps only the recently opened so-called "Action Coffee Shop." Mr. Funahashi Seiichi, who claims to be an activist writer, even made such a desperate cry:

"...Although activism has been ordered to withdraw from collectivism here, there is still a long and enduring life in the spirit of activism, which will be a great guiding force for Japanese literature in the future. On this point, even if it suffers a setback in the morning or evening, it cannot die. On the contrary, it can be said that the future is shining with hopeful light. The spiritual state of this young generation will continue to develop without any damage. Why? Because cultural control is currently prevalent, and the tasks of cultural protection, technological value, academic freedom, and the defense of the intellectual class are forcing the Japanese intellectuals in all aspects, so the task of activism is even greater. But finally, what I want to say is that activism is not just a literary school that creates action-oriented new social novels for private novels, but a greater literary spirit, and an attitude of integrity from writers in distress."

This activism, which has become a homeless dog, will probably be difficult to revive even if it cries out like this unless it changes its ways.

The Advance of Verbatim Literature

Regarding the advocacy of verbatim literature, I once introduced it in this publication. At that time, what was introduced was only the basis for the emergence of verbatim literature and the theory of creation. But now this movement has expanded even further, and even a magazine called "Verbatim Literature" has been published. The original members were Kimura Ki, Kishi Sanji, Tamura Eitaro, Sakamura Seiji, Iwasaki Sakae, Sasamoto Tora, and Kataoka Ko. New members include Kaionji Chogoro, Togawa Sadao, and Toyoshima Kaoru. Naturally, these people all have their own interpretations of verbatim literature, and their motivations for participating are also different.

Kimura Ki interprets verbatim literature from his usual standpoint of biographical novels, and he is also engaged in biographical literary work, starting with "Rai Sanyo."

Kishi Sanji, as an advocate of verbatim literature, has written many essays. One is the elimination of the vulgarity of popular literature, and the other is the issue of popularizing literature. His work is "Ishida Mitsunari." This work is now being staged at the Tsukiji Little Theater as a performance commemorating the first anniversary of the New Cooperative Theater Company.

Iwasaki Sakae wrote a verbatim novel called "Tenpo Chushingura." It is about a peasant uprising that occurred in Dewa.

Iwamoto Tora faithfully depicts the cross-section of the history of the Meiji Restoration with "Kaishu and the Masseuse" and "The Red-Light District at the End of the幕末 Period."

Kataoka Ko wrote "Iron Guns and Tsurukichi" from the standpoint of verbatim literature, and he also wrote an essay "The Process to Verbatim Literature," stipulating the theory of verbatim literature as follows:

"Rectifying the errors of traditionally popular historical records, vigorously appealing to the public's interest in knowledge, needless to say, this is the standpoint of historical literature. But history is not something that is dead and on the other shore, it is the content of us today. To treat it as something dead is only for archaeologists. If you want to know the past, you must know the present; if you want to know the present, you must know the history of the past. Although this is contradictory, true historical literature that depicts modern human beings emerges from the mutual understanding of these two things. Moreover, as long as it is literature, the writer's imagination and fantasy cannot be lightly dismissed. Not only that, but the writer's imagination and fantasy can also infinitely move towards the gaps in the historical records that have been distorted and buried. As long as the historical view is sound..."

Although this is Mr. Kataoka's personal opinion, it can also be said to be the overall opinion, because the opposition to vulgar and obscene entertainment reading, the emphasis on historical truth, the giving of modern interpretations, and the demand for simple expression are the reasons for the members' common agreement.

Since its inception in the spring, the Verbatim Literature Research Association has not yet produced any significant major works in addition to the achievements mentioned above. However, due to the emergence of the magazine "Verbatim Literature," we can conclude that it will flourish recently.

Describing Nature by Qu Yi

Here, the so-called person who studies immortality is actually a person who studies nature. It is said that the death of a person who studies nature is not called death, but 物化 [wù huà, transformation of things]. Because he is a part of nature, and nature has its transactions; his death is merely a change in nature. It is not really death, because the existence or non-existence of the body cannot be used as a rule for life and death. The so-called "dust and dirt" can also "mold Yao and Shun into one." Only by studying the "divine person on Mount Miaogushe, who does not eat grains, drinks wind and dew, rides on clouds and controls flying dragons, and travels beyond the four seas, whose spirit is concentrated, so that things are not diseased... even if there are great floods that reach the sky, they will not drown him, and even if there is a great drought, metal and stone will flow, and earthen mountains will be scorched but not hot," can one achieve the ultimate goal. This is the unified personality of nature and man that they seek. The highest goal of nature worshipers is to pursue this unified personality.

However, in reality, the so-called unification is by no means the surrender of one side to the other, completely eliminating the individuality of one side and conforming to the individuality of the other. The unified personality pursued by nature worshipers is rather the elimination of one's own personality and conforming to the rule of nature. This is not unification, but destruction. True unification must be in the heroic struggle between man and nature. The so-called "change" in the Book of Changes means this. The Tuan says: "Water and fire counteract each other, and two women live together, but their wills cannot be united, so it is called change. Change is believed, civilization is explained, and great success is achieved with righteousness. Change is appropriate, and regret will disappear. Heaven and earth change, and the four seasons are formed. Tang and Wu made revolutions, which conformed to Heaven and responded to man. The time of change is great!" Because change is the unity of opposites, it is evolution. Nature has its own unity of opposites, evolving into the four seasons; man and nature also have their unity of opposites, which is completed in revolution. Nature worshipers, in their essence, forget their own existence and have never established a correct relationship with nature. Consequently, when reflected in literature, it is bound to be full of the spirit of pantheism. The spirit of pantheism in the description of nature in literature is not only very obvious in Chinese literature, but also very prosperous in European literature in the nineteenth century. We can easily understand this by picking someone at random.

For example, the English Lake Poet Wordsworth, in his collection of lyrical poems, almost entirely sings of nature. Rainbows, daffodils, skylarks, butterflies, cuckoos, primroses on rocks, springs, robin redbreasts chasing butterflies, etc., what he sings of are all things in the natural world, and he entrusts them with feelings of praise, almost like the Chinese pastoral poet Tao Qian. Coleridge said that in the first year he worked with Wordsworth, they often used the two major elements of poetry as the subject of their conversations, namely, faithfully depicting the truth of nature to make the reader sympathize, and arousing strange interest by using the changing colors of imagination. These are the two kinds of power in their poetry. He also said: "In Wordsworth, the purpose of writing poetry is to arouse the attention of people under the anesthesia of habit, to call people to feel the beauty and mystery of the world in front of us, to feel the wonder of everyday things, and to arouse a kind of supernatural feeling" (see Coleridge: Biographia literaria). The so-called supernatural feeling here is the idea of God. It can be seen that his attitude towards nature is pantheistic. His short poem "Rainbow" says it like this:

"My heart leaps up when I behold

A rainbow in the sky:

So was it when my life began;

So is it now I am a man;

So be it when I shall grow old,

Or let me die!

The Child is father of the Man;

And I could wish my days to be

Bound each to each by natural piety."

Also, in "Lines Composed a Few Miles above Tintern Abbey"

For I have learned

To look on nature, not as in the hour

Of thoughtless youth; but hearing oftentimes

The still, sad music of humanity,

Nor harsh nor grating, though of ample power

To chasten and subdue. And I have felt

A presence that disturbs me with the joy

Of elevated thoughts; a sense sublime

Of something far more deeply interfused,

Whose dwelling is the light of setting suns,

And the round ocean and the living air,

And the blue sky, and in the mind of man;

A motion and a spirit, that impels

All thinking things, all objects of all thought,

And rolls through all things. Therefore am I still

A lover of the meadows and the woods,

And mountains; and of all that we behold

From this green earth; of all the mighty world

Of eye and ear,—both what they half create,

And what perceive; well pleased to recognise

In nature and the language of the sense,

The anchor of my purest thoughts, the nurse,

The guide, the guardian of my heart, and soul

Of all my moral being."

From these poems, nature, God, and eternity have already become a trinity; only man is small and momentary. But is man really small and momentary? No, human history shows that man is by no means as weak and incompetent as the poet imagines. In many places, man is the master of nature, the creator of nature. It is man who introduces the electricity in nature into proper use. It is man who gives appropriate regulation to the light and heat in nature. Only those who can bravely look directly at the human world can also correctly understand nature and correctly establish the relationship between man and nature. Therefore, even if he is not born in an era when human power can overcome nature, if he is a singer of human life, he will never surrender to nature or bow down before nature. The Tang Dynasty poet Du Fu, no matter how much suffering he went through, did not worship nature as a god in his poems, because he was unwilling to escape the human world and go to the bosom of nature to seek the comfort of nature, let alone deify nature. The nature he describes in his poems is all placed under the power of man. For example: "How is Mount Tai? The green of Qi and Lu is endless. The magic of creation gathers its beauty, and yin and yang split the dawn. Stirring the chest, clouds rise from the layers, and the eyes tear as birds return. I will ascend to the summit and overlook all the mountains." This shows the attitude that even with the magic of nature, human power is enough to overcome it. Even if not, he writes about nature because of people and events, as a kind of background. For example, a poem in Qiang Village says: "The red clouds are towering in the west. The setting sun is level with the ground. The thatched door is filled with birds and sparrows, and the returning traveler has traveled a thousand miles. Wife and children are surprised that I am here, and after the shock, they wipe away their tears. The world is chaotic and suffered a great disaster, and it is accidental that I have returned alive. Neighbors fill the walls, sighing and sobbing. The night is late and the candle is lit, and we look at each other as if in a dream." Another example is Baisha Ferry: "The perilous road follows the Yangtze River, and the ferry is at the bottom of a steep bank. The boats are staggered, and the people are like clouds in the sky. The sky is closed outside the wilderness, and it is late in the middle of the stream. My horse neighs to the north, and the mountain monkeys call to each other. The water is clear and the stones are rugged, and the sand is white and the beach is vast. I wash away my sorrows and pains, and I am relieved of my many diseases. The high walls stand against the steep cliffs, and the turbulent waves are even more chaotic. Facing the wind, I still turn my head and sigh three times." There is no deification of nature in any of these. As in Baisha Ferry, the poem shows the posture of the struggle between man and nature. Or else, he returns nature to its original appearance. For example, the poem "Wild Hope": "The clear autumn looks boundless, and the distant shadows rise. The distant water is clear and clean, and the lonely city is hidden in the mist. The leaves are sparse and the wind blows them down, and the mountains turn and the sun first sets. Why does the solitary crane return so late? The dusk crows are already filling the forest."

Life Sketches by Jie Ren

When I was little, I often loved to run to the beach to catch crabs. I don't know how many times I was scolded by my mother for catching crabs, because I always came back covered in mud. It was always a disappointing thing to be scolded after returning home excitedly with crabs. But scolding is scolding, I still go to catch crabs. That stubbornness made my loving mother suffer a lot.

But I have to say, this is mostly because my home is too close to the beach. When I go out to play, I unconsciously play on the beach. When I saw those crabs walking sideways, I naturally had the idea of catching them back, so I started to catch them.

Each time, in addition to getting covered in mud, I also brought back a can of prisoners. Those things were imprisoned together in the can, climbing frantically, trying to break out of this cage. The sharp claws scratched the iron can, making a rattling sound, as if preparing to break through it. But where could they escape to? They were still in that iron can. Seeing this, I smiled triumphantly. As for how to dispose of those things? Sometimes I kept them in a small jar, but keeping that kind of thing was meaningless after all, because that kind of crab didn't have a delicious taste that you could chew on, so before long, I lost interest and threw them away. Sometimes I played with them, arbitrarily putting them to death, and I was like a demon king wielding the power of life and death. Now, when I think back to my cruel mood at that time, I can't help but be horrified. But thinking carefully, that's also very common. There are many things in human society that are ten thousand times more cruel than this! This is still a small matter.

Speaking of the method of catching, it is very simple and also very clever. How do you catch those living things? It is only with a hemp rope. The method is to first make a noose at one end of the rope, and put it on the mouth of the crab hole. The person silently ambushes behind the rope. Once the crab's body is exposed at the mouth of the hole, immediately pull the hemp rope with force, and the crab is immediately pulled out of the hole. At that time, even if it is half dead from the fall, it will be dizzy and not know the east, west, south, or north. To be honest, it is fine if you don't fall into that noose, but once you fall into that noose, you don't have to think about escaping.

This trick is very similar to the "tripping rope" often mentioned in old novels. Many heroes and good men often fall into the tripping rope, so that they have no use for their martial arts. Thinking of the crab being caught, isn't it the same? However, people who are accustomed to using this kind of trick are ultimately despicable and unworthy!

Now I am an adult, and I have been muddling through in this society, so that kind of plaything has naturally been abandoned, and I will no longer have that kind of interest. But I still often think, I am even more aware that I am also a crab now! In front of me, there are many nooses, waiting for me to jump in. Or will my fate be even more terrible than that of the crab?

Noble's Wine, Poor's Tears by Huang Shiying

No One Knows (1) by Hugh Walpole, translated by He Wei

George Willard glanced around very quickly. He got up from the desk in the office of the Winesburg Eagle and ran out through the back door in a hurry. The night was warm and dark. Although it was not yet eight o'clock, the alley behind the newspaper office was already pitch black. A group of mules tied to wooden stakes in the nearby darkness were trampling on the hard, muddy ground. A cat jumped out from George Willard's feet and fled into the night. The young man was a little timid. He had been doing things all day as if he had been knocked unconscious. In the alley, he trembled as if frightened.

In the darkness, George Willard walked along the alley very vigilantly. The back doors of the Winesburg shops were still open, and he could see people sitting under the lights. The landlady of the hotel, Mrs. Willie, was standing next to the counter of the Maplebaum Toy Store, with a basket hanging on her arm. Serving her was the clerk, Curt Grimm. He was leaning against the counter, speaking very attentively.

George Willard crouched down and jumped over the light that spilled out from the doorway. He began to run in the darkness. Behind the hotel of Ed Griffith, Gilly Boter, the town's old drunkard, was sleeping soundly on the ground. He staggered across the drunk's outstretched leg, laughing intermittently.

He had already started an adventure. All day he had been trying to make up his mind to carry out this adventure, and now he had already started. Since six o'clock, he had been sitting in the office of the Winesburg Eagle thinking about this matter.

But he had not made a decision. He just jumped up, hurried past Will Heyde, who was doing proofreading in the composing room, and ran along the alley.

George Willard ran across one street after another. He avoided the people who passed by him. He crossed many streets one after another. When he ran past a street lamp, he pulled down his hat to cover his face. He dared not think. There was a kind of terror in his heart, but it was fresh. He was afraid that the adventure he had started would be hindered, that he would lose courage, and that he would retreat.

He found Louise Trunnion in the kitchen of her father's house. She was close to a kerosene lamp, washing dishes. She was standing behind the lattice door in the small, shed-like kitchen at the back of the house. George Willard stopped against a fence, trying to stop his body from trembling. Only a potato field separated him from Munson's. After five minutes, he was able to bring himself to call her. "Louise! Oh, Louise!" he called. The call choked in his throat, and his voice became a hoarse whisper.

Shen Bao Local Supplement: Discussing the Flattery of Officials by Chui

Officials were called parents in the autocratic era, but in the Republican era, they are public servants. Parents can be flattered, but public servants do not need to be flattered. However, although the political system has changed, the customs remain. If you don't believe me, please look at the recent ban from the Henan Provincial Government. Not only is Henan like this, but I think other provinces are also like this.

Recently, the Henan Provincial Government stated that the gentry and people of various counties often fabricate false words to publish in newspapers for the current county magistrate, praising his merits and virtues, or establishing monuments to his virtuous administration. Even some county government officials are also listed among them, hoping to gain favor with their superiors. Whenever the county magistrate is transferred, they falsely borrow names and make excuses to retain him, which is actually overstepping their authority, interfering, and corrupting officialdom. Therefore, a special order has been issued to all counties to strictly investigate and prohibit such actions.

Flattering officials was originally a kind of social skill between officials and gentry, so flattering officials is not necessarily an evil act. However, the first condition is that the official must be good, and the gentry must also be good. However, good officials are not easy to obtain. If they are good officials, they do not want people to flatter them. And good gentry are also not easy to obtain. If they are good gentry, they will definitely not be willing to flatter officials. Therefore, flattering officials is a kind of collusion between officials and gentry, deceiving superiors and oppressing subordinates.

Officials use the power of the gentry to embezzle and pervert the law, and the gentry use the authority of officials to exploit the people. Therefore, officials and gentry become united, and the local area suffers greatly. Because if officials do not have the gentry as their accomplices, they dare not do evil. If the gentry do not have the officials as their protectors, they also dare not do evil. When officials and gentry unite, then embezzlement, perversion of the law, and exploitation of the people can be done without any restrictions. Therefore, Sun Yat-sen wanted to overthrow the local tyrants and evil gentry and eradicate the corrupt officials, precisely because of this reason, because the gentry will not be greedy without officials, and the gentry will not be evil without officials.

Originally, there were only the people below the officials, and only the officials above the people. Now, another kind of class is created between the officials and the people, called the gentry. What is this for? In the Manchu Qing Dynasty, there were retired high officials and scholars who had passed the imperial examinations. In terms of their qualifications, they surpassed the common people. In terms of their official rank, they had no duties. Calling them gentry or scholars was perhaps appropriate. Now it is the Republican era. Those who are in office are officials, and those who are retired are common people. There is no such thing as gentry. The so-called gentry today are flies and dogs, their power is overwhelming, they are neither officials nor people, and they monopolize litigation and exploit the people. This is the business that such people specialize in.

Since the Republic of China, how many years has it been? The more the evil gentry are suppressed, the more they become. The more the corrupt officials are eradicated, the more severe they become. The reason why our country's politics cannot be clear and the local order is increasingly corrupt is because of this reason. Therefore, there are those who praise the merits and virtues of the current officials, and there are those who build monuments to the virtuous administration of the officials who are about to leave office. This kind of flattering situation fully demonstrates the evidence of collusion between officials and gentry. Therefore, if the local tyrants and evil gentry are not eradicated, the corrupt officials will never disappear. If the corrupt officials do not disappear, how can we hope for clear politics?

Eastern Travel Notes by Ice Flow

Living in Tokyo

Friends, now I want to talk to you about living in Tokyo. I guarantee that you will find this interesting if you come. We are usually accustomed to living in Shanghai's Sino-Western houses. Once we run to Japan and see these completely different houses, we will definitely find them interesting, although sometimes you will feel a lot of inconvenience.

We all know that Japan is often hit by earthquakes and storms, so except for banks, department stores, agency offices, and the residences of a few capitalists, they are all low wooden houses. The roofs are also made of corrugated iron instead of tiles to reduce the danger. In this way, even if the house collapses, it is much safer than a brick and tile house. However, this kind of wooden house can last for a hundred years or more, because their wood is strong and will not corrode even after being exposed to rain. At the same time, the people who live there are very careful. Their walls are made of paper, and the doors are made of a piece of glass and thin paper. When we walk inside and close the door, we find that we are surrounded by paper walls and cannot find a way out. In fact, every paper wall is a door. We live in this place, so we must be very careful. When we first come, we really feel unaccustomed. If we are not careful, we will poke a hole in the wall.

Inside the house, the floor is covered with mats. They calculate the size of the house in units of how many mats. The room is empty. There are no tables, benches, or beds. What there is, is only a low table that is not even a foot high. That is used for eating. Reading and writing are also done here. On the wall of each room, there is a "closet." We put all the boxes, clothes, and bedding inside. At night, we take them out to sleep. Usually, we close the door, and it is the same as the wall. Some houses have a shrine, which the Japanese treat with the utmost respect. If we sit with our buttocks facing it, they will be unhappy.

There is also something that we are not accustomed to, and that is wearing shoes. It is not necessary to say that we have to take off our shoes as soon as we enter the door. Even inside the house, we have to wear several pairs of slippers. Because there are mats in the room, we are of course barefoot. When we leave the room to go to the aisle, we have to wear slippers. For example, when we go from the second floor to the toilet downstairs, we have to change slippers three times: one pair when we go down the stairs, we cannot wear them when we pass through the dining room downstairs, and we have to wear another pair after passing through the dining room. We have to change another pair when we enter the toilet. It is really too much trouble, but if we don't do this, we cannot keep the room clean.

In Tokyo, Chinese students have three kinds of places to live: boarding houses, rented rooms, and rented houses. A boarding house is a kind of hotel. You must eat their meals. It usually costs about 30 yuan per month. There are maids to serve you. It is not worthwhile for people who are not very financially well off, but it is of great benefit for learning Japanese. At the same time, as long as you pay the money every month, you can live in peace and quiet. Living in a rented room is different. First, it is not easy to rent a room. Upper-class people do not rent out empty rooms. Middle-class people would rather leave them empty than rent them to Chinese people. What is left are only lower-class people. These houses are either in a bad environment, or the landlady is very naggy. It is especially difficult for people who have just arrived in Tokyo, because they do not understand Japanese. Even if they find a house that they are not very satisfied with, they still have to put up with some anger. The landlord will look you up and down and ask you everything, even asking you if you have "bedbugs" on you. When you hear this, you are sure to get angry. However, after you move in, she will feel that you are not annoying, and she will treat you well, like family. If you have minor ailments such as a cold, she will take care of you carefully and comfort you in every way. This is very different from the iron faces of Shanghai's Er Yongdong. What is not restricted is living in a rented house. Rented houses in the city are too expensive, so people usually live outside the city. It only costs about 20 yuan per month, and it is really cheap to live with three or four people. However, Chinese people are uninhibited, and they often still drink and gamble until midnight because there is no restriction. Even if they don't do this, because everyone has their own friends, people come and go, and it is difficult to get satisfactory results. Therefore, if you cannot find like-minded close friends, living in a rented house is also unsuccessful.

The Depressed Market by Le Jian

In the early morning and afternoon, on this yellow mud open space, the noisy sounds are swirling, and the honest and simple people are bustling about, making it the hottest and most lively market in the day.

It is still an ancient-style market, with many small stalls set up with single canopies and tents. The furnishings are shabby. It seems to be a "guerrilla" style business, which can be moved at any time and can also set up a storefront at any time. In the prehistoric era, this kind of convenient design was very suitable. There are also many shops that have already built thatched huts, which are very simple. The soil on the walls is peeling off in pieces. Even more, there are even entire walls that have collapsed. That must be because the plasterers cut corners.

I often see several men carrying a fir tree to block those walls that are tilting as if they are about to collapse, or tapping lightly with a hammer, the crisp sound echoing clearly. I often see people nailing broken reed mats on the cracks in the walls to resist the wind, rain, and sunlight. Every time I see their declining situation, my heart is always inexplicably melancholy, and I really admire their loyal attitude towards seeking a living.

Even if there are two lively markets every day, this yellow mud open space is always depressed, making a person who is not accustomed to this kind of life feel curious and hesitant.

In the early morning, I always have to walk out of my dirty house and step on the cattle urine and horse dung path to the vast outside to take a walk, smelling the refreshing air, and at the same time going to the market for a tour - the bustling morning market.

Hanging on the meat stalls are bloody pig heads, sheep heads, and cow tails. On the cutting board are pieces of beef, wrapped in white cloth. The beef is still trembling slightly. Next to it are placed sharp knives. I realize that using these sharp knives to cut the soft beef should give a smooth feeling of pleasure.

There are people patronizing the chicken vendors, and the fat chickens in the cage are being poked east and west with a wooden stick, being carefully selected. The chicken vendors stare with both eyes, seeing that the customers are just poking, looking a bit annoyed, knocking the scale pole straight on the chicken cage, knocking, knocking. Somehow, maybe just by accident, a chicken jumped out, hobbling with two short legs straight towards the open space, crowing loudly.

Two people catch the chicken, many people join in the fun, and the yellow mud dust flies up.

The chicken vendor pinches a bamboo pole, his body hunched over like a bow. Rather than saying he is catching the chicken, it is better to say he is beating the chicken. But in this way, the entire market is in an uproar, and the sound of laughter is even more noisy. But soon it subsides, and the wave of excitement also subsides. The occasional passersby have the mood of Ecclesiastes.

From time to time, there is unrestrained laughter from the teahouses, choking in the thatched huts without windows.

Then, the wandering people who travel around the world come again, carrying a load of black and old broken boxes, a large bundle of spears, swords, arrows, and the like, and also carrying a pair of strange urns, stopping in the center of the open space, and then beating the big gong and leather drum, and the spears are already dancing.

"Killing the son and putting him in the urn, killing the son and putting him in the urn! Come on!" A group of children gathered together stumbling, shouting, and the leather drum beat even harder!

I have been standing on this open space for a long time, and I start to step blankly on a small path of cattle urine and horse dung to go home, and my heart cannot help but be depressed and melancholy.

"The depressed market! The depressed market!"

On a Raft of Logs by Lei Tieming

I spent a night on a floating raft of logs…

The setting sun had long since sunk into the sea, and the faint red afterglow of the setting sun on the vast sea was gradually losing its luster, dyeing the water where the sea and sky meet into a patch of twilight black.

The tide was flowing quietly, smiling, constantly receding towards the east.

There were countless rafts of logs. Three rafts of logs were tied together into one section, and every five or six zhang was another section. On each section of rafts of logs stood two Malay men. They slowly punted with long poles, and the rafts of logs flowed down with the water, gradually disappearing behind the distant jungle.

The two punters on the raft of logs I jumped on were a young man named Jizhi and Ama Cai, who liked to drink. At this time, he silently put the bamboo pole on his shoulder and pushed hard.

"Be careful, if the water is shallow in the small harbor, we will have to spend the night."

Jizhi raised his sturdy black back, pushing with the bamboo pole and saying this. Then he raised his eyes, which had experienced wind and rain, and glanced at me.

"The tide won't recede that fast," I said.

Our raft of logs entered the small harbor. The trees and vines on both sides of the small harbor seemed to deliberately narrow the harbor. The water was only five feet deep, but it was flowing rapidly with a sound…

At night, the wind in June blew through the sparse trees, and the falling leaves fell on the water and on the raft of logs with a rustling sound.

Ama Cai lit the earthen oil lamp made from a wine bottle, and the smoky smell filled the air. The orange-yellow light illuminated the thin, black faces of everyone on the raft of logs.

We let the raft of logs drift by itself, turned back, put out the last half-pot of cold rice, and sat around smiling, grabbing and eating with washed fingers. We clamped skewers of salted fish with branches, coated them with soy sauce and chili, and roasted them by the stove.

The rows of rafts of logs flowed down the rapids like a long snake…

These rafts of logs were all collected from the forest. The Malay workers punted non-stop, passing through long and winding mountain streams, and then flowing into this calm sea. They spent the night on the beach, and endured the rain and sun on the rafts of logs, just drifting day and night, working constantly, until they safely punted each raft of logs to the lumber yard.

The water in the harbor flowed narrowly in bends, shallower and faster than before. The rafts of logs bumped against the weeds on the shore, and the weeds fell down with a cry. The branches on both sides of the bank were short and intertwined, and the black harbor seemed like a deep mountain cave.

The lights on the rafts of logs in front and behind were blocked by the trees, and they could not see each other. Their ears could only hear the constant sound of punting and the sparse low voices.

"Hey, we're here!"…

The shout came from the raft of logs in front, and then it spread to the last section. Laughter and songs rippled in the small harbor. Labor was joyfully accelerated, and melodious marches seemed to leak out from every dark corner of the forest.

"Haha, we're here…"

"Jizhi, is it almost dawn!"

I was so happy that I almost shed tears. The hot wind whistled lightly in the treetops, the flame spit out from the mouth of the wine bottle shook wildly, and a glittering wave of light surged on the water.

Handing Over Work by De Min

Nature of Sino-Japanese Economic Cooperation: Primarily Civilian-Led, Specific Measures Undetermined; North China Economic Association Not Involved by Government 47

Sino-Japanese Businessmen Decide to Establish Sino-Japanese Trade Association

(Nanjing) Regarding Sino-Japanese economic cooperation, Japanese sources report that the South Manchuria Railway Company is largely responsible. According to external sources, it will mainly be civilian-led. Specific measures will be formulated after our economic survey mission returns home and presents its opinions. The North China Economic Association has already been established. It is understood that the nature of the association is purely a people's organization, and the government is not involved. (Central News Agency telegram, 22nd)

(Tokyo) On the 22nd, the Chinese survey mission and Japanese business leaders held another cordial discussion and decided to establish the Sino-Japanese Trade Association. Preparatory personnel from both sides will, based on the regulations, convene the founding members for a meeting before mid-November. The regulations are as follows: (1) The association will be called the Sino-Japanese Trade Association in China and the Japan-China Trade Association in Japan. (2) The purpose of the association is to jointly study the economic conditions of China and Japan and promote trade between the two countries. (3) The association will establish general headquarters in Shanghai, China, and Tokyo, Japan, respectively. However, when necessary, branch offices may be established in important commercial ports in China and Japan with the resolution of each board of directors. (4) The members of the association shall be Chinese and Japanese individuals engaged in industry and related fields. (5) Applicants for membership in the association must be introduced by two or more members and approved by the board of directors of the general headquarters in their country of residence. (6) The Shanghai and Tokyo general headquarters will each have a president. The president of the Shanghai general headquarters will be elected from among the executive directors by the Chinese members. The president of the Tokyo general headquarters will be elected from among the executive directors by the Japanese members. Each general headquarters will have two vice presidents, one Chinese and one Japanese. At the Shanghai general headquarters, the Chinese vice president will be elected from among the executive directors. The Japanese vice president will be concurrently held by the president of the Tokyo general headquarters. At the Tokyo general headquarters, the Japanese vice president will be elected from among the executive directors. The Chinese vice president will be concurrently held by the president of the Shanghai general headquarters. However, each concurrently appointed vice president may appoint a resident representative to perform duties on their behalf. (7) The Shanghai and Tokyo general headquarters will each have no more than 25 directors, elected by the members from among the members at the general meeting, with a term of three years, eligible for re-election. (8) Each general headquarters will elect no more than seven executive directors from among the directors. (9) Each general headquarters may establish a number of councilors, each recommended by the directors of the general headquarters. (10) The association may establish various specialized committees as necessary for its affairs. (11) The association will hold a general meeting of members once a year, alternately in China or Japan. The date and location of the meeting will be agreed upon by the two boards of directors. The association may convene an extraordinary general meeting of members after consultation between the two boards of directors in the event of special events. The meeting cannot be held without the attendance of more than one-third of the total number of members, and no resolution can be passed without the consent of more than half of the members present. If a member is unable to attend the general meeting of members due to unavoidable circumstances, they may entrust another member as a representative. The general meeting of members will be convened jointly by the presidents of the two general headquarters. (12) Each board of directors will hold a regular meeting once a month, convened by each president. (13) The expenses of the association will be covered by membership fees and special donations. (14) Membership fees shall be twelve yuan per person per year, based on the currency of the country of residence, payable in one lump sum. (15) The budget and final accounts of the association shall be submitted by the two boards of directors to the general meeting of members for review and approval. (16) These regulations shall be implemented after being resolved by the general meeting of members. If amendments are necessary, they may be proposed by the two boards of directors to the general meeting of members for resolution and amendment. (17) The regulations of the branch offices of the association and various detailed rules of the general and branch offices shall be formulated and implemented by the two boards of directors in consultation. Supplementary provisions: (1) The first general meeting of members will be replaced by the meeting of founding members held simultaneously in Shanghai and Tokyo. (2) The first directors will be elected from among the founding members. (Koku-Bunsha News Agency, 22nd)

The Tangshan Public Security Bureau has issued an order to its subordinates to strictly arrest them. (Special dispatch, 22nd)

Rebellion of Nitrate Bandits in Pingxiang Has Been Suppressed 53

(Tianjin) The Changlu Salt Transport Commissioner's Office received a telegram from Sun Dequan, commander of the division stationed in Daming, stating that the rebellion of nitrate bandits in Pingxiang has been suppressed and the bandits have been disbanded. (Special dispatch, 22nd)

(Tianjin) According to sources from the Changlu Transport Office, the nitrate bandits in Pingxiang were incited by Shi Yousan and Liu Guitang to form the Universal Alliance Red Cross. Li Xiu and a certain Zhang were the leaders. Anyone with a gun who joined would receive a monthly salary of eight yuan. The method of raising funds was to apportion it to salt farmers household by household. They already had many machine guns and rifles. A few days ago, the tax police stationed in Yongnian were transferred and passed through bandit territory. The bandits mistakenly thought they were going to suppress them, so they opened fire and were defeated. However, they are lurking in various places and have the potential to make a comeback. (Special dispatch, 22nd)

Legislative Yuan to Hold Temporary Meeting Today to Review the Draft Constitutional Amendment 54

(Nanjing) The Legislative Yuan is scheduled to hold a temporary meeting at 2:00 PM on the 24th to review the draft constitutional amendment. Sun Ke, Fu Bingchang, etc., are scheduled to return to the east from Shanghai on the evening of the 22nd to preside over the revised constitution. In addition to being deleted and merged into eight chapters, the number of articles has also been reduced by 20 and one new article has been added. There are now 149 articles remaining. The deleted articles are mostly those originally in the deleted fiscal and military chapters and similar implementing law articles in other non-deleted chapters. The added article stipulates that the implementation matters stipulated in the Constitution shall be determined by law separately when necessary. According to sources familiar with the matter, all the deletions in this revision of the draft constitution are based on the revision principles and attachments issued by the central government. The retained articles have been passed through the three readings of the Legislative Yuan. The added article is only one and is also added in accordance with the central government's revision principles. It is expected that the Yuan meeting will only make technical modifications to the amendment. According to well-informed sources, the amendment will not include provisions in the fundamental law of the country that are similar to the articles of the implementing law. It is planned that the restrictions on the right to be elected for the president, vice president, and provincial governors will not be stipulated in the Constitution. (Central News Agency telegram, 22nd)

Coastal Areas Prepare to Protect the Yellow River Embankment; Guanxian Conscripts Labor to Reinforce the Yanhe River Embankment 55

(Xuzhou) Commissioner Hao Guoxi recently ordered the magistrates of Donghai, Shuyang, and Guanyun counties that since the Yellow River embankments in each county have been rushed to completion by the entire county's conscripts, they must ensure that the project is completed and strong enough to resist the raging waves. After the completion, when the laborers return, if no one is responsible for guarding the embankments and no emergency response organization is prepared, danger is inevitable. They should be planned in advance to ensure thoroughness. The counties have all been assigned responsibilities for guarding after receiving the order. (Central News Agency telegram, 22nd)

(Xuzhou) The Haizhou Commissioner's Office believes that the Yellow River dike in Donghai has been rushed to completion with the strength of the entire county and should be protected with greater efforts. It specifically ordered the county government to divide the dike into sections for defense to avoid danger. Now, the Qianshui in Xinpu is rising again. It is expected that the Shuishui dam in the Central Canal will be opened, and even if the rivers in Haizhou rise, it should not cause trouble. (Special dispatch, 22nd)

(Xuzhou) According to Haixun News, the new dike at Daikou, on the Yanhe River outside the west gate of Guanyun, has loose soil. On the night of the 18th, it was breached by the wind and waves for four zhang. Laborers rushed to block the breach overnight, and fortunately, no danger occurred. However, the entire Yanhe River dike is newly built, and cracks appear from time to time. The Guanxian County Government ordered 1,500 laborers from the first district to rush to reinforce it to prevent further rises before the breach is blocked upstream. (Special dispatch, 22nd)

Hydraulic Experts Pu Deli and Others Return to Nanjing; Xianghe River Closure Plan to First Build a Remote Embankment; Requires More Than 2 Million Yuan, Scheduled to Begin Construction 56

(Nanjing) Pu Deli, consultant of the Hydraulic Department of the National Economic Council, and Section Chief Wang Huzhen returned to Nanjing by plane from Hankou on the afternoon of the 22nd and reported to the association about their visit to Hankou. It is said that after Xi Dejiong became the director of the Yangtze River and Han River Engineering Bureau, he first paid attention to the Xiang River closure project and proposed three plans, requesting the National Economic Council to send personnel to participate in opinions. After our arrival in Hankou, we reviewed the plans proposed by the bureau one by one and invited representatives from relevant agencies in Hankou to discuss them at length. It was unanimously agreed that the plan to build a remote embankment between Luohan Temple and Jiukou in Zhongxiang was the most appropriate. The plan requires more than 2.4 million in construction costs. The Jianghan Engineering Bureau has already submitted the plan charts to the National Economic Council for approval. It has also sent personnel to Zhongxiang to prepare for the project. It is planned to conscript 80,000 workers from Zhongxiang, Tianmen, Jingyou, and other counties and start construction on November 1st. (Central News Agency telegram, 22nd)

(Baoding) According to a telegram from Qi Shouan and others, the Hebei Construction Department said on the 22nd that the conditions of sections two and three of the southern project have been greatly affected by the pumping of the Linpukou Gate, resulting in sudden changes in dangerous points. The brick dam is being defended as it is being threatened, and Lengzhai is being directly impacted by the fierce current, becoming increasingly dangerous. Hubei Conscripts Labor for Service; Engineering Plans Have Been Determined 60

(Hankou) Hubei's conscription of labor for service is about to be implemented. Various engineering plans have been determined by the provincial government: 1. Repairing embankments: The total length of embankments in the province is approximately 2,000 kilometers, requiring 15 million cubic meters of earthwork and 30 million man-days. Areas with minor disasters will be compensated at no cost, while areas with severe disasters will be compensated at 30 cents per cubic meter for main embankments and half for civil embankments. 2. Repairing roads: new lines are designated as Yi Shi Lai, Er Yang Qi, San Yang Luo, and repairing the old Bai and other highways. (Special dispatch, 22nd)

Guangdong Construction Bonds Rescheduled for Issuance 64

(Nanjing) Because the Guangdong Provincial Government has not been able to catch up with the handling of the Guangdong Construction Bonds, originally scheduled to be issued on August 1st, they have requested the Executive Yuan to change the issuance date to December 1st, and change the interest payment dates from the end of January and July to the end of May and November. The date for the lottery redemption will also be changed from January 15th and July 15th to May 15th and November 15th. The Executive Yuan submitted the matter to the Ministry of Finance for review, and the Ministry of Finance reported to the Executive Yuan that it should be approved. (Central News Agency telegram, 22nd)
